Gemma 2B on 7.NS.A.2

Common Core Standard 7.NS.A.2

This standard covers the following:

Apply and extend previous understandings of multiplication and division and of fractions to multiply and divide rational numbers.

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: Calculate the product of (29/2) and (19/28) and write your answer as a simplified fraction.

Gemma 2B: 

To find the product of \(\frac{29}{2}\) and \(\frac{19}{28}\), we multiply the numerators together and the denominators together:

\[
\frac{29}{2} \times \frac{19}{28} = \frac{29 \times 19}{2 \times 28}
\]

First, calculate the numerator:

\[
29 \times 19 = 551
\]

Next, calculate the denominator:

\[
2 \times 28 = 56
\]

So, the product is:

\[
\frac{551}{56}
\]

To check if this fraction can be simplified, we need to determine if there are any common factors between 551 and 56. 

The prime factorization of 551 is:
\[
551 = 19 \times 29
\]

The prime factorization of 56 is:
\[
56 = 2^3 \times 7
\]

Since there are no common factors between 551 and 56, the fraction \(\frac{551}{56}\) is already in its simplest form.

### Answer: \(\frac{551}{56}\)

Expected answer: 551/56

Correct? Yes

ðŸ”— Follow-up

Problem: After finding the product of (29/2) and (19/28), multiply your result by (8/28). Write your final answer as a simplified fraction.

Gemma 2B: 

First, we already found the product of \(\frac{29}{2}\) and \(\frac{19}{28}\) to be \(\frac{551}{56}\).

Next, we need to multiply this result by \(\frac{8}{28}\):

\[
\frac{551}{56} \times \frac{8}{28} = \frac{551 \times 8}{56 \times 28}
\]

First, calculate the new numerator:

\[
551 \times 8 = 4408
\]

Next, calculate the new denominator:

\[
56 \times 28 = 1568
\]

So, the product is:

\[
\frac{4408}{1568}
\]

To simplify this fraction, we need to find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 4408 and 1568. We can use the Euclidean algorithm to find the GCD.

1. Divide 4408 by 1568 and find the remainder:
\[
4408 \div 1568 \approx 2.81 \quad \text{(integer part is 2)}
\]
\[
4408 - 2 \times 1568 = 4408 - 3136 = 1272
\]

2. Now, divide 1568 by 1272 and find the remainder:
\[
1568 \div 1272 \approx 1.23 \quad \text{(integer part is 1)}
\]
\[
1568 - 1 \times 1272 = 1568 - 1272 = 296
\]

3. Next, divide 1272 by 296 and find the remainder:
\[
1272 \div 296 \approx 4.29 \quad \text{(integer part is 4)}
\]
\[
1272 - 4 \times 296 = 1272 - 1184 = 88
\]

4. Now, divide 296 by 88 and find the remainder:
\[
296 \div 88 \approx 3.36 \quad \text{(integer part is 3)}
\]
\[
296 - 3 \times 88 = 296 - 264 = 32
\]

5. Next, divide 88 by 32 and find the remainder:
\[
88 \div 32 \approx 2.75 \quad \text{(integer part is 2)}
\]
\[
88 - 2 \times 32 = 88 - 64 = 24
\]

6. Now, divide 32 by 24 and find the remainder:
\[
32 \div 24 \approx 1.33 \quad \text{(integer part is 1)}
\]
\[
32 - 1 \times 24 = 32 - 24 = 8
\]

7. Finally, divide 24 by 8 and find the remainder:
\[
24 \div 8 = 3 \quad \text{(integer part is 3)}
\]
\[
24 - 3 \times 8 = 24 - 24 = 0
\]

Since the remainder is now 0, the GCD of 4408 and 1568 is 8.

Now, we can simplify the fraction \(\frac{4408}{1568}\) by dividing both the numerator and the denominator by their GCD, which is 8:

\[
\frac{4408 \div 8}{1568 \div 8} = \frac{551}{196}
\]

### Answer: \(\frac{551}{196}\)

Expected answer: 551/196

Correct? Yes

Gemma 2B:

So, the product is:

To check if this fraction can be simplified, we need to determine if there are any common factors between 551 and 28.

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: Calculate the result of the following problem: multiply 7 by the result of dividing 27 by 12. Write your answer as a simplified fraction.

Gemma 2B: 

First, we need to divide 27 by 12. 

\[
\frac{27}{12}
\]

Next, we simplify the fraction by finding the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 27 and 12. The GCD of 27 and 12 is 3. We divide both the numerator and the denominator by 3:

\[
\frac{27 \div 3}{12 \div 3} = \frac{9}{4}
\]

Now, we need to multiply 7 by \(\frac{9}{4}\):

\[
7 \times \frac{9}{4} = \frac{7 \times 9}{4} = \frac{63}{4}
\]

The fraction \(\frac{63}{4}\) is already in its simplest form.

### Answer: \(\frac{63}{4}\)

Expected answer: 63/4

Correct? Yes

ðŸ”— Follow-up

Gemma 2B: 

First, we need to divide 26 by 12.

\[
\frac{26}{12}
\]

Next, we simplify the fraction by finding the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 26 and 12. The GCD of 26 and 12 is 2. We divide both the numerator and the denominator by 2:

\[
\frac{26 \div 2}{12 \div 2} = \frac{13}{6}
\]

Now, we need to multiply 7 by \(\frac{13}{6}\):

\[

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: Susan has a recipe that calls for 30 parts of flour to 27 parts of water. If she decides to use 29 parts of flour instead, and she keeps the water proportion the same, how much water will she use? Calculate this using fraction multiplication: ((30 / 30) * (29 / 27)).

Gemma 2B: 

To determine how much water Susan will use if she adjusts the flour to 29 parts while keeping the same proportion, we can use the given ratio and set up a proportion.

The original ratio of flour to water is 30 parts of flour to 27 parts of water. This can be written as:
\[ \frac{30}{27} \]

If Susan uses 29 parts of flour instead, we need to find the corresponding amount of water, \( x \), that maintains the same ratio:
\[ \frac{30}{27} = \frac{29}{x} \]

We can solve for \( x \) by cross-multiplying:
\[ 30x = 27 \times 29 \]

First, calculate \( 27 \times 29 \):
\[ 27 \times 29 = 783 \]

Now, solve for \( x \):
\[ 30x = 783 \]
\[ x = \frac{783}{30} \]
\[ x = 26.1 \]

Thus, Susan will use 26.1 parts of water.

### Answer: 26.1

Expected answer: 29/27

Correct? No

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: Calculate the result of the following operation: ((24 / 22) * (24 / 17)). Write your answer as a simplified fraction.

Gemma 2B: 

To solve the expression \(\left(\frac{24}{22}\right) \times \left(\frac{24}{17}\right)\), we first multiply the numerators and the denominators separately:

\[
\frac{24}{22} \times \frac{24}{17} = \frac{24 \times 24}{22 \times 17}
\]

Next, we calculate the products:

\[
24 \times 24 = 576
\]
\[
22 \times 17 = 374
\]

So, the expression becomes:

\[
\frac{576}{374}
\]

To simplify this fraction, we need to find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 576 and 374. We can use the Euclidean algorithm to find the GCD.

1. Divide 576 by 374 and find the remainder:
\[
576 \div 374 \approx 1 \quad \text{(quotient)} \quad \text{remainder} = 576 - 374 = 202
\]

2. Now, divide 374 by 202 and find the remainder:
\[
374 \div 202 \approx 1 \quad \text{(quotient)} \quad \text{remainder} = 374 - 202 = 172
\]

3. Next, divide 202 by 172 and find the remainder:
\[
202 \div 172 \approx 1 \quad \text{(quotient)} \quad \text{remainder} = 202 - 172 = 30
\]

4. Now, divide 172 by 30 and find the remainder:
\[
172 \div 30 \approx 5 \quad \text{(quotient)} \quad \text{remainder} = 172 - 150 = 22
\]

5. Next, divide 30 by 22 and find the remainder:
\[
30 \div 22 \approx 1 \quad \text{(quotient)} \quad \text{remainder} = 30 - 22 = 8
\]

6. Now, divide 22 by 8 and find the remainder:
\[
22 \div 8 \approx 2 \quad \text{(quotient)} \quad \text{remainder} = 22 - 16 = 6
\]

7. Next, divide 8 by 6 and find the remainder:
\[
8 \div 6 \approx 1 \quad \text{(quotient)} \quad \text{remainder} = 8 - 6 = 2
\]

8. Finally, divide 6 by 2 and find the remainder:
\[
6 \div 2 \approx 3 \quad \text{(quotient)} \quad \text{remainder} = 6 - 6 = 0
\]

Since the remainder is now 0, the GCD of 576 and 374 is 2.

We can now simplify the fraction \(\frac{576}{374}\) by dividing both the numerator and the denominator by their GCD, which is 2:

\[
\frac{576 \div 2}{374 \div 2} = \frac{288}{187}
\]

Thus, the simplified fraction is:

### Answer: \(\frac{288}{187}\)

Expected answer: 288/187

Correct? Yes

ðŸ”— Follow-up

Problem: After finding the result of ((24 / 22) * (24 / 17)) in the previous problem, multiply the answer you found by (27 / 18). Write the result as a simplified fraction.

Gemma 2B: 

We start with the simplified fraction from the previous problem, which is \(\frac{288}{187}\). We need to multiply this by \(\frac{27}{18}\):

\[
\frac{288}{187} \times \frac{27}{18}
\]

First, we multiply the numerators and the denominators:

\[
\frac{288 \times 27}{187 \times 18}
\]

Next, we calculate the products:

\[
288 \times 27 = 7776
\]
\[
187 \times 18 = 3366
\]

So, the expression becomes:

\[
\frac{7776}{3366}
\]

To simplify this fraction, we need to find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 7776 and 3366. We can use the Euclidean algorithm to find the GCD.

1. Divide 7776 by 3366 and find the remainder:
\[
7776 \div 3366 \approx 2 \quad \text{(quotient)} \quad \text{remainder} = 7776 - 6732 = 1044
\]

2. Now, divide 3366 by 1044 and find the remainder:
\[
3366 \div 1044 \approx 3 \quad \text{(quotient)} \quad \text{remainder} = 3366 - 3132 = 234
\]

3. Next, divide 1044 by 234 and find the remainder:
\[
1044 \div 234 \approx 4 \quad \text{(quotient)} \quad \text{remainder} = 1044 - 936 = 108
\]

4. Now, divide 234 by 108 and find the remainder:
\[
234 \div 108 \approx 2 \quad \text{(quotient)} \quad \text{remainder} = 234 - 216 = 18
\]

5. Finally, divide 108 by 18 and find the remainder:
\[
108 \div 18 \approx 6 \quad \text{(quotient)} \quad \text{remainder} = 108 - 108 = 0
\]

Since the remainder is now 0, the GCD of 7776 and 3366 is 18.

We can now simplify the fraction \(\frac{7776}{3366}\) by dividing both the numerator and the denominator by their GCD, which is 18:

\[
\frac{7776 \div 18}{3366 \div 18} = \frac{432}{187}
\]

Thus, the simplified fraction is:

### Answer: \(\frac{432}{187}\)

Expected answer: 432/187

Correct? Yes

ðŸ”— Follow-up

Problem: Since the previous problem had you evaluating ((24 / 22) * (24 / 17)), consider this change: What if instead of multiplying (24 / 22) by (24 / 17), you multiplied it by (24 / 9)? Calculate the result of ((24 / 22) * (24 / 9)) and write your answer as a simplified fraction.

Gemma 2B: 

To solve the expression \(\left(\frac{24}{22}\right) \times \left(\frac{24}{9}\right)\), we first multiply the numerators and the denominators separately:

\[
\frac{24}{22} \times \frac{24}{9} = \frac{24 \times 24}{22 \times 9}
\]

Next, we calculate the products:

\[
24 \times 24 = 576
\]
\[
22 \times 9 = 198
\]

So, the expression becomes:

\[
\frac{576}{198}
\]

To simplify this fraction, we need to find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 576 and 198. We can use the Euclidean algorithm to find the GCD.

1. Divide 576 by 198 and find the remainder:
\[
576 \div 198 \approx 2 \quad \text{(quotient)} \quad \text{remainder} = 576 - 2 \times 198 = 576 - 396 = 180
\]

2. Now, divide 198 by 180 and find the remainder:
\[
198 \div 180 \approx 1 \quad \text{(quotient)} \quad \text{remainder} = 198 - 180 = 18
\]

3. Next, divide 180 by 18 and find the remainder:
\[
180 \div 18 \approx 10 \quad \text{(quotient)} \quad \text{remainder} = 180 - 180 = 0
\]

Since the remainder is now 0, the GCD of 576 and 198 is 18.

We can now simplify the fraction \(\frac{576}{198}\) by dividing both the numerator and the denominator by their GCD, which is 18:

\[
\frac{576 \div 18}{198 \div 18} = \frac{32}{11}
\]

Thus, the simplified fraction is:

### Answer: \(\frac{32}{11}\)

Expected answer: 32/11

Correct? Yes

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: What is the result when you divide 25/4 by 16/6? Please write your answer as a simplified fraction.

Gemma 2B: 

To solve the problem of dividing \( \frac{25}{4} \) by \( \frac{16}{6} \), we need to multiply \( \frac{25}{4} \) by the reciprocal of \( \frac{16}{6} \).

First, find the reciprocal of \( \frac{16}{6} \):
\[ \text{Reciprocal of } \frac{16}{6} = \frac{6}{16} \]

Now, multiply \( \frac{25}{4} \) by \( \frac{6}{16} \):
\[ \frac{25}{4} \times \frac{6}{16} = \frac{25 \times 6}{4 \times 16} = \frac{150}{64} \]

Next, simplify \( \frac{150}{64} \) by finding the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 150 and 64. The GCD of 150 and 64 is 2.

Divide both the numerator and the denominator by their GCD:
\[ \frac{150 \div 2}{64 \div 2} = \frac{75}{32} \]

Thus, the simplified fraction is:
### Answer: \(\frac{75}{32}\)

Expected answer: 75/32

Correct? Yes

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: Determine the result of the following: Multiply the fraction 3/7 by the fraction 26/6 and express your answer as a simplified fraction.

Gemma 2B: 

To determine the result of multiplying the fractions \(\frac{3}{7}\) and \(\frac{26}{6}\), we follow these steps:

1. Multiply the numerators together:
   \[
   3 \times 26 = 78
   \]

2. Multiply the denominators together:
   \[
   7 \times 6 = 42
   \]

So, the product of the fractions is:
\[
\frac{78}{42}
\]

Next, we need to simplify this fraction. To do this, we find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 78 and 42.

The prime factorization of 78 is:
\[
78 = 2 \times 3 \times 13
\]

The prime factorization of 42 is:
\[
42 = 2 \times 3 \times 7
\]

The common factors are 2 and 3. Therefore, the GCD of 78 and 42 is:
\[
2 \times 3 = 6
\]

We divide both the numerator and the denominator by their GCD (6):
\[
\frac{78 \div 6}{42 \div 6} = \frac{13}{7}
\]

Thus, the simplified fraction is:
\[
\frac{13}{7}
\]

### Answer: \(\frac{13}{7}\)

Expected answer: 13/7

Correct? Yes

ðŸ”— Follow-up

Problem: In the previous question, you found the result of (3 / 7) * (26 / 6). Now, take that result and multiply it by the fraction 23/2. What's the result of this calculation, expressed as a simplified fraction?

Gemma 2B: 

We previously found that \(\frac{3}{7} \times \frac{26}{6} = \frac{13}{7}\).

Now, we need to multiply this result by \(\frac{23}{2}\):

\[
\frac{13}{7} \times \frac{23}{2}
\]

To multiply these fractions, we multiply the numerators together and the denominators together:

1. Multiply the numerators:
   \[
   13 \times 23 = 299
   \]

2. Multiply the denominators:
   \[
   7 \times 2 = 14
   \]

So, the product of the fractions is:
\[
\frac{299}{14}
\]

Since 299 and 14 have no common factors other than 1, the fraction \(\frac{299}{14}\) is already in its simplest form.

### Answer: \(\frac{299}{14}\)

Expected answer: 299/14

Correct? Yes

ðŸ”— Follow-up

Problem: In the previous problem, you multiplied the fraction 3/7 by the fraction 26/6. Now, let's change the fraction a bit. Instead of 3/7, use 7/7 (which is actually 1). Multiply this new fraction 7/7 by the same fraction 26/6. What is the result of this new calculation, expressed as a simplified fraction?

Gemma 2B: 

To determine the result of multiplying the fractions \(\frac{7}{7}\) and \(\frac{26}{6}\), we follow these steps:

1. Multiply the numerators together:
   \[
   7 \times 26 = 182
   \]

2. Multiply the denominators together:
   \[
   7 \times 6 = 42
   \]

So, the product of the fractions is:
\[
\frac{182}{42}
\]

Next, we need to simplify this fraction. To do this, we find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 182 and 42.

The prime factorization of 182 is:
\[
182 = 2 \times 7 \times 13
\]

The prime factorization of 42 is:
\[
42 = 2 \times 3 \times 7
\]

The common factors are 2 and 7. Therefore, the GCD of 182 and 42 is:
\[
2 \times 7 = 14
\]

We divide both the numerator and the denominator by their GCD (14):
\[
\frac{182 \div 14}{42 \div 14} = \frac{13}{3}
\]

Thus, the simplified fraction is:
\[
\frac{13}{3}
\]

### Answer: \(\frac{13}{3}\)

Expected answer: 13/3

Correct? Yes

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: Calculate the result of the expression (17 / 10) * (28 / 10) and write your answer in decimal form.

Gemma 2B: 

To solve the expression \((\frac{17}{10}) \times (\frac{28}{10})\), we first multiply the numerators and then the denominators:

\[
\frac{17 \times 28}{10 \times 10}
\]

Next, we calculate the product of the numerators:

\[
17 \times 28 = 476
\]

And the product of the denominators:

\[
10 \times 10 = 100
\]

So, the expression becomes:

\[
\frac{476}{100}
\]

To convert this fraction to decimal form, we divide the numerator by the denominator:

\[
\frac{476}{100} = 4.76
\]

### Answer: 4.76

Expected answer: 119/25

Correct? Yes

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: Determine the value of the given expression: ((29 / 14) * (23 / 6))

Gemma 2B: 

To determine the value of the given expression \(\left(\frac{29}{14}\right) \times \left(\frac{23}{6}\right)\), we follow these steps:

1. Multiply the numerators together:
   \[
   29 \times 23 = 667
   \]

2. Multiply the denominators together:
   \[
   14 \times 6 = 84
   \]

3. Combine the results to form the fraction:
   \[
   \frac{667}{84}
   \]

4. Simplify the fraction if possible. We need to check if 667 and 84 have any common factors other than 1. 

   - The prime factorization of 667 is \(667 = 23 \times 29\).
   - The prime factorization of 84 is \(84 = 2^2 \times 3 \times 7\).

Since there are no common factors between 667 and 84, the fraction \(\frac{667}{84}\) is already in its simplest form.

### Answer: \(\frac{667}{84}\)

Expected answer: 667/84

Correct? Yes

ðŸ”— Follow-up

Problem: The value of the expression ((29 / 14) * (23 / 6)) was calculated in the previous problem. Now, calculate the result of multiplying the previously found value by (21 / 21).

Gemma 2B: 

To calculate the result of multiplying the previously found value \(\frac{667}{84}\) by \(\frac{21}{21}\), we follow these steps:

1. Write the expression:
   \[
   \left(\frac{667}{84}\right) \times \left(\frac{21}{21}\right)
   \]

2. Multiply the numerators together:
   \[
   667 \times 21 = 14007
   \]

3. Multiply the denominators together:
   \[
   84 \times 21 = 1764
   \]

4. Combine the results to form the fraction:
   \[
   \frac{14007}{1764}
   \]

5. Simplify the fraction if possible. We need to check if 14007 and 1764 have any common factors.

   - The prime factorization of 14007 is \(14007 = 3^2 \times 7 \times 223\).
   - The prime factorization of 1764 is \(1764 = 2^2 \times 3^2 \times 7^2\).

   The greatest common divisor (GCD) of 14007 and 1764 is \(3^2 \times 7 = 63\).

6. Divide both the numerator and the denominator by their GCD (63):
   \[
   \frac{14007 \div 63}{1764 \div 63} = \frac{222}{28}
   \]

7. Simplify further if possible:
   - The prime factorization of 222 is \(222 = 2 \times 3 \times 37\).
   - The prime factorization of 28 is \(28 = 2^2 \times 7\).

   The GCD of 222 and 28 is 2.

8. Divide both the numerator and the denominator by their GCD (2):
   \[

   \]

Problem: A cargo ship carries 28/21 of its capacity in the morning, and 22/4 of its capacity in the afternoon. If the cargo in the morning represents the load allocated to consumer goods and the cargo in the afternoon represents industrial supplies, what is the total fractional representation of these two types of cargo hauled in one day? Calculate ((28 / 21) * (22 / 4)). Write your answer as a simplified fraction.

Gemma 2B: 

To find the total fractional representation of the cargo hauled in one day, we need to add the fractions representing the cargo in the morning and the afternoon.

First, let's simplify each fraction:

1. Simplify \( \frac{28}{21} \):
   \[
   \frac{28}{21} = \frac{28 \div 7}{21 \div 7} = \frac{4}{3}
   \]

2. Simplify \( \frac{22}{4} \):
   \[
   \frac{22}{4} = \frac{22 \div 2}{4 \div 2} = \frac{11}{2}
   \]

Next, we need to add these two fractions. To do this, we need a common denominator. The least common multiple of 3 and 2 is 6.

Convert each fraction to have a denominator of 6:
\[
\frac{4}{3} = \frac{4 \times 2}{3 \times 2} = \frac{8}{6}
\]
\[
\frac{11}{2} = \frac{11 \times 3}{2 \times 3} = \frac{33}{6}
\]

Now, add the fractions:
\[
\frac{8}{6} + \frac{33}{6} = \frac{8 + 33}{6} = \frac{41}{6}
\]

Thus, the total fractional representation of the cargo hauled in one day is:
\[
\frac{41}{6}
\]

Problem: Determine the result of the following mathematical expression: (16 / 4) / (24 / 21). Write your answer as a simplified fraction or decimal.

Gemma 2B: 

To determine the result of the expression \((16 / 4) / (24 / 21)\), we will follow these steps:

1. Simplify the numerator and the denominator separately.
2. Divide the simplified numerator by the simplified denominator.

First, simplify the numerator:
\[ 16 / 4 = 4 \]

Next, simplify the denominator:
\[ 24 / 21 \]

To simplify \( 24 / 21 \), we can divide both the numerator and the denominator by their greatest common divisor (GCD), which is 3:
\[ 24 / 21 = (24 \div 3) / (21 \div 3) = 8 / 7 \]

Now, we need to divide the simplified numerator by the simplified denominator:
\[ 4 / (8 / 7) \]

Dividing by a fraction is equivalent to multiplying by its reciprocal:
\[ 4 \times (7 / 8) \]

Perform the multiplication:
\[ 4 \times 7 = 28 \]
\[ 28 / 8 \]

Simplify \( 28 / 8 \) by dividing both the numerator and the denominator by their GCD, which is 4:
\[ 28 / 8 = (28 \div 4) / (8 \div 4) = 7 / 2 \]

Thus, the result of the expression \((16 / 4) / (24 / 21)\) is:
### Answer: 7/2

Expected answer: 7/2

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: Calculate the result of the following product of fractions: (15 / 13) * (19 / 7). Make sure to write your answer as a simplified fraction.

Gemma 2B: 

To calculate the product of the fractions \(\frac{15}{13} \times \frac{19}{7}\), we multiply the numerators together and the denominators together:

\[
\frac{15}{13} \times \frac{19}{7} = \frac{15 \times 19}{13 \times 7}
\]

First, we calculate the product of the numerators:

\[
15 \times 19 = 285
\]

Next, we calculate the product of the denominators:

\[
13 \times 7 = 91
\]

So, the product of the fractions is:

\[
\frac{285}{91}
\]

To simplify this fraction, we need to find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 285 and 91. We can use the Euclidean algorithm to find the GCD.

1. Divide 285 by 91 and find the remainder:
\[
285 \div 91 = 3 \quad \text{remainder} \quad 285 - 3 \times 91 = 12
\]

2. Now, divide 91 by 12 and find the remainder:
\[
91 \div 12 = 7 \quad \text{remainder} \quad 91 - 7 \times 12 = 7
\]

3. Next, divide 12 by 7 and find the remainder:
\[
12 \div 7 = 1 \quad \text{remainder} \quad 12 - 1 \times 7 = 5
\]

4. Now, divide 7 by 5 and find the remainder:
\[
7 \div 5 = 1 \quad \text{remainder} \quad 7 - 1 \times 5 = 2
\]

5. Next, divide 5 by 2 and find the remainder:
\[
5 \div 2 = 2 \quad \text{remainder} \quad 5 - 2 \times 2 = 1
\]

6. Finally, divide 2 by 1:
\[
2 \div 1 = 2 \quad \text{remainder} \quad 2 - 2 \times 1 = 0
\]

Since the remainder is now 0, the GCD is the last non-zero remainder, which is 1. Therefore, the fraction \(\frac{285}{91}\) is already in its simplest form.

### Answer: \(\frac{285}{91}\)

Expected answer: 285/91

Correct? Yes

We already calculated the multiplication of \(\frac{14}{10}\) by \(\frac{30}{5}\) and found it to be \(\frac{42}{5}\).

Now, we need to multiply this result by \(\frac{13}{15}\):

\[
\frac{42}{5} \times \frac{13}{15} = \frac{42 \times 13}{5 \times 15}
\]

Calculate the products:

\[
42 \times 13 = 546
\]
\[
5 \times 15 = 75
\]

So, we have:

\[
\frac{546}{75}
\]

Next, we simplify the fraction by finding the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 546 and 75. The GCD of 546 and 75 is 3.

Now, divide both the numerator and the denominator by their GCD:

\[
\frac{546 \div 3}{75 \div 3} = \frac{182}{25}
\]

Thus, the simplified fraction is:

\[
\frac{182}{25}
\]

### Answer: \(\frac{182}{25}\)

Expected answer: 182/25

\[
\frac{26}{1} \times \frac{14}{29}
\]

Next, we perform the multiplication of the fractions:
\[
\frac{26 \times 14}{1 \times 29} = \frac{364}{29}
\]

Now, we simplify the fraction \(\frac{364}{29}\). We perform the division:
\[
364 \div 29 = 12.55

\[

Problem: Evaluate the expression ((24 / 11) * (27 / 26)) and write your answer as a simplified fraction.

Gemma 2B:

1. Multiply the numerators together:
   \[
   24 \times 27 = 648
   \]

2. Multiply the denominators together:
   \[
   11 \times 26 = 286
   \]

So, the expression becomes:
\[
\frac{648}{286}
\]

Next, we need to simplify this fraction. We do this by finding the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 648 and 286.

First, we find the prime factorizations of both numbers:
- 648: \(648 = 2^3 \times 3^4\)
- 286: \(286 = 2 \times 11 \times 13\)

The common factor is 2.

Now, divide both the numerator and the denominator by their GCD (which is 2):
\[
\frac{648 \div 2}{286 \div 2} = \frac{324}{143}
\]

Since 324 and 143 have no common factors other than 1, the fraction \(\frac{324}{143}\) is in its simplest form.

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: Find the solution to the following multiplication problem: Multiply the fraction 26/9 by the fraction 17/13. Write your answer in simplest form.

Gemma 2B: 

To solve the multiplication of the fractions \(\frac{26}{9}\) and \(\frac{17}{13}\), we follow these steps:

1. Multiply the numerators together:
   \[
   26 \times 17 = 442
   \]

2. Multiply the denominators together:
   \[
   9 \times 13 = 117
   \]

So, the product of the fractions is:
\[
\frac{442}{117}
\]

Next, we need to simplify this fraction. We do this by finding the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 442 and 117.

First, we use the Euclidean algorithm to find the GCD:
- Divide 442 by 117, which gives a quotient of 3 and a remainder of 91:
  \[
  442 = 117 \times 3 + 91
  \]
- Next, divide 117 by 91, which gives a quotient of 1 and a remainder of 26:
  \[
  117 = 91 \times 1 + 26
  \]
- Then, divide 91 by 26, which gives a quotient of 3 and a remainder of 13:
  \[
  91 = 26 \times 3 + 13
  \]
- Finally, divide 26 by 13, which gives a quotient of 2 and a remainder of 0:
  \[
  26 = 13 \times 2 + 0
  \]

Since the remainder is now 0, the GCD is the last non-zero remainder, which is 13.

Now, we divide both the numerator and the denominator of \(\frac{442}{117}\) by their GCD, 13:
\[
\frac{442 \div 13}{117 \div 13} = \frac{34}{9}
\]

Thus, the simplified form of the product is:
\[
\frac{34}{9}
\]

### Answer: \(\frac{34}{9}\)

Expected answer: 34/9

Correct? Yes

ðŸ”— Follow-up

  \[
  816 = 270 \times 3 + 6
  \]
- Next, divide 270 by 6, which gives a quotient of 45 and a remainder of 0:

Since the remainder is now 0, the GCD is the last non-zero remainder, which is 6.

Now, we divide both the numerator and the denominator of \(\frac{816}{270}\) by their GCD, 6:

Gemma 2B: 

To solve the multiplication of the fractions \(\frac{25}{9}\) and \(\frac{17}{13}\), we follow these steps:

1. Multiply the numerators together:
   \[
   25 \times 17 = 425
   \]

2. Multiply the denominators together:
   \[
   9 \times 13 = 117
   \]

So, the product of the fractions is:
\[
\frac{425}{117}
\]

Next, we need to simplify this fraction. We do this by finding the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 425 and 117.

First, we use the Euclidean algorithm to find the GCD:
- Divide 425 by 117, which gives a quotient of 3 and a remainder of 74:
  \[
  425 = 117 \times 3 + 74
  \]
- Next, divide 117 by 74, which gives a quotient of 1 and a remainder of 43:
  \[
  117 = 74 \times 1 + 43
  \]
- Then, divide 74 by 43, which gives a quotient of 1 and a remainder of 31:
  \[
  74 = 43 \times 1 + 31
  \]
- Next, divide 43 by 31, which gives a quotient of 1 and a remainder of 12:
  \[
  43 = 31 \times 1 + 12
  \]
- Then, divide 31 by 12, which gives a quotient of 2 and a remainder of 7:
  \[
  31 = 12 \times 2 + 7
  \]
- Finally, divide 12 by 7, which gives a quotient of 1 and a remainder of 5:
  \[
  12 = 7 \times 1 + 5
  \]
- Continue dividing 7 by 5, which gives a quotient of 1 and a remainder of 2:
  \[
  7 = 5 \times 1 + 2
  \]
- Finally, divide 5 by 2, which gives a quotient of 2 and a remainder of 1:
  \[
  5 = 2 \times 2 + 1
  \]
- Lastly, divide 2 by 1, which gives a quotient of 2 and a remainder of 0:
  \[
  2 = 1 \times 2 + 0
  \]

Since the remainder is now 0, the GCD is the last non-zero remainder, which is 1.

Since the GCD is 1, the fraction \(\frac{425}{117}\) is already in its simplest form.

Problem: Solve the following problem: What is the result of the expression (28 / 16) / (27 / 24)? Write your answer as a simplified fraction.

Gemma 2B: 

To solve the expression \(\frac{28}{16} \div \frac{27}{24}\), we can use the property of division of fractions, which states that dividing by a fraction is equivalent to multiplying by its reciprocal. Therefore, we can rewrite the expression as:

\[
\frac{28}{16} \div \frac{27}{24} = \frac{28}{16} \times \frac{24}{27}
\]

Next, we simplify the fractions before multiplying. 

First, simplify \(\frac{28}{16}\):
\[
\frac{28}{16} = \frac{28 \div 4}{16 \div 4} = \frac{7}{4}
\]

Next, simplify \(\frac{24}{27}\):
\[
\frac{24}{27} \text{ is already in its simplest form.}
\]

Now, multiply the simplified fractions:
\[
\frac{7}{4} \times \frac{24}{27} = \frac{7 \times 24}{4 \times 27} = \frac{168}{108}
\]

Finally, simplify \(\frac{168}{108}\):
\[
\frac{168}{108} = \frac{168 \div 12}{108 \div 12} = \frac{14}{9}
\]

Thus, the result of the expression \(\frac{28}{16} \div \frac{27}{24}\) is:

### Answer: \(\frac{14}{9}\)

Expected answer: 14/9

Correct? Yes

Problem: The local bakery was making a special order for a customer. The recipe they are using requires 19/28, and they want to make exactly 30/4 of this recipe. How much of the ingredient will they require?

Gemma 2B: 

To determine how much of the ingredient the bakery will require, we need to multiply the amount required for one recipe by the number of recipes they want to make.

The recipe requires \( \frac{19}{28} \) of the ingredient, and they want to make \( \frac{30}{4} \) of this recipe.

First, simplify \( \frac{30}{4} \):
\[ \frac{30}{4} = \frac{15}{2} \]

Now, multiply \( \frac{19}{28} \) by \( \frac{15}{2} \):
\[ \frac{19}{28} \times \frac{15}{2} = \frac{19 \times 15}{28 \times 2} = \frac{285}{56} \]

To simplify \( \frac{285}{56} \), we check for any common factors. The greatest common divisor (GCD) of 285 and 56 is 1, so the fraction is already in its simplest form.

Thus, the bakery will require \( \frac{285}{56} \) of the ingredient.

### Answer: \(\frac{285}{56}\)

Expected answer: 285/56

Correct? Yes

Problem: Calculate the result of the following multiplication of fractions operation: (9 / 7) * (25 / 30). Express your answer as a simplified fraction.

Gemma 2B: 

To solve the multiplication of the fractions \(\frac{9}{7} \times \frac{25}{30}\), we follow these steps:

1. Multiply the numerators together:
\[ 9 \times 25 = 225 \]

2. Multiply the denominators together:
\[ 7 \times 30 = 210 \]

So, the product of the fractions is:
\[ \frac{225}{210} \]

Next, we simplify the fraction by finding the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 225 and 210.

The prime factorization of 225 is:
\[ 225 = 3^2 \times 5^2 \]

The prime factorization of 210 is:
\[ 210 = 2 \times 3 \times 5 \times 7 \]

The common factors are 3 and 5. Therefore, the GCD is:
\[ 3 \times 5 = 15 \]

Now, we divide both the numerator and the denominator by their GCD:
\[ \frac{225 \div 15}{210 \div 15} = \frac{15}{14} \]

Thus, the simplified fraction is:
\[ \frac{15}{14} \]

ðŸ”— Follow-up

Problem: After finding the result of ((21 / 9) * (29 / 6)), consider what would have happened if the initial calculation involved (21 / 9) instead of (11 / 9). Calculate the new result and write your answer as a simplified fraction.

Gemma 2B: 

To solve the problem \(\left(\frac{21}{9}\right) \times \left(\frac{29}{6}\right)\), we first multiply the numerators together and the denominators together.

First, multiply the numerators:
\[ 21 \times 29 = 609 \]

Next, multiply the denominators:
\[ 9 \times 6 = 54 \]

So, the product of the fractions is:
\[ \frac{609}{54} \]

To simplify this fraction, we need to find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 609 and 54. We can use the Euclidean algorithm to find the GCD.

1. Divide 609 by 54:
\[ 609 \div 54 = 11 \text{ remainder } 15 \]
So, \( 609 = 54 \times 11 + 15 \).

2. Now, find the GCD of 54 and 15:
\[ 54 \div 15 = 3 \text{ remainder } 9 \]
So, \( 54 = 15 \times 3 + 9 \).

3. Next, find the GCD of 15 and 9:
\[ 15 \div 9 = 1 \text{ remainder } 6 \]
So, \( 15 = 9 \times 1 + 6 \).

4. Now, find the GCD of 9 and 6:
\[ 9 \div 6 = 1 \text{ remainder } 3 \]
So, \( 9 = 6 \times 1 + 3 \).

5. Finally, find the GCD of 6 and 3:
\[ 6 \div 3 = 2 \text{ remainder } 0 \]
So, \( 6 = 3 \times 2 + 0 \).

Since the remainder is now 0, the GCD is the last non-zero remainder, which is 3.

Now, we divide both the numerator and the denominator of \(\frac{609}{54}\) by their GCD, which is 3:
\[ \frac{609 \div 3}{54 \div 3} = \frac{203}{18} \]

### Answer: \(\frac{203}{18}\)

Expected answer: 203/18

Correct? Yes

Problem: Calculate the result of the following problem and write your answer as a simplified fraction: ((29 / 2) / (23 / 19))

Gemma 2B: 

To solve the problem \(\left(\frac{29}{2}\right) \div \left(\frac{23}{19}\right)\), we need to follow these steps:

1. **Rewrite the division as multiplication by the reciprocal:**
   \[
   \left(\frac{29}{2}\right) \div \left(\frac{23}{19}\right) = \left(\frac{29}{2}\right) \times \left(\frac{19}{23}\right)
   \]

   \[

   \]
   \[
   2 \times 23 = 46
   \]

4. **Form the new fraction:**
   \[
   \frac{551}{46}
   \]

5. **Simplify the fraction if possible:**
   - Check for common factors between 551 and 46. Since 551 is a prime number and 46 is not a factor of 551, the fraction is already in its simplest form.

### Answer: \(\frac{551}{46}\)

Expected answer: 551/46

Correct? Yes

ðŸ”— Follow-up

Problem: After calculating the result of ((29 / 2) / (23 / 19)), multiply your answer by (29 / 18). Write your final answer as a simplified fraction.

Gemma 2B: 

First, we start with the result from the previous calculation:
\[
\left(\frac{29}{2}\right) \div \left(\frac{23}{19}\right) = \frac{551}{46}
\]

Next, we need to multiply this result by \(\frac{29}{18}\):
\[
\frac{551}{46} \times \frac{29}{18}
\]

To multiply these fractions, we multiply the numerators together and the denominators together:
\[
\frac{551 \times 29}{46 \times 18}
\]

Calculate the products:
\[
551 \times 29 = 15979
\]
\[
46 \times 18 = 828
\]

So, the fraction becomes:
\[
\frac{15979}{828}
\]

Now, we need to simplify this fraction. We check for the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 15979 and 828. Using the Euclidean algorithm:

1. \(15979 \div 828 \approx 19\) remainder \(307\)
2. \(828 \div 307 \approx 2\) remainder \(214\)
3. \(307 \div 214 \approx 1\) remainder \(93\)
4. \(214 \div 93 \approx 2\) remainder \(28\)
5. \(93 \div 28 \approx 3\) remainder \(9\)
6. \(28 \div 9 \approx 3\) remainder \(1\)
7. \(9 \div 1 = 9\) remainder \(0\)

The GCD is 1, meaning the fraction \(\frac{15979}{828}\) is already in its simplest form.

\]

\]

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: Calculate the product of the fractions 11/19 and 22/7. Write your answer as a simplified fraction.

Gemma 2B: 

To find the product of the fractions \( \frac{11}{19} \) and \( \frac{22}{7} \), we multiply the numerators together and the denominators together:

\[
\frac{11}{19} \times \frac{22}{7} = \frac{11 \times 22}{19 \times 7}
\]

First, calculate the numerator:

\[
11 \times 22 = 242
\]

Next, calculate the denominator:

\[
19 \times 7 = 133
\]

So, the product of the fractions is:

\[
\frac{242}{133}
\]

To simplify this fraction, we need to find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 242 and 133. We can use the Euclidean algorithm to find the GCD:

1. Divide 242 by 133, which gives a quotient of 1 and a remainder of 109:
   \[
   242 = 133 \times 1 + 109
   \]

2. Divide 133 by 109, which gives a quotient of 1 and a remainder of 24:
   \[
   133 = 109 \times 1 + 24
   \]

3. Divide 109 by 24, which gives a quotient of 4 and a remainder of 13:
   \[
   109 = 24 \times 4 + 13
   \]

4. Divide 24 by 13, which gives a quotient of 1 and a remainder of 11:
   \[
   24 = 13 \times 1 + 11
   \]

5. Divide 13 by 11, which gives a quotient of 1 and a remainder of 2:
   \[
   13 = 11 \times 1 + 2
   \]

6. Divide 11 by 2, which gives a quotient of 5 and a remainder of 1:
   \[
   11 = 2 \times 5 + 1
   \]

7. Finally, divide 2 by 1, which gives a quotient of 2 and a remainder of 0:
   \[
   2 = 1 \times 2 + 0
   \]

Since the remainder is now 0, the GCD is the last non-zero remainder, which is 1. Therefore, the fraction \( \frac{242}{133} \) is already in its simplest form.

### Answer: \(\frac{242}{133}\)

Expected answer: 242/133

Correct? Yes

\]

So, the product of the fractions is:

To simplify this fraction, we need to find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 6050 and 532. We can use the Euclidean algorithm to find the GCD:

1. Divide 6050 by 532, which gives a quotient of 11 and a remainder of 258:
   \[
   6050 = 532 \times 11 + 258
   \]

The common factor is 3.

\[ \frac{399 \div 3}{150 \div 3} = \frac{133}{50} \]

\[ \frac{133}{50} \]

Gemma 2B: 

To solve the problem \(\frac{28}{1} \div \frac{30}{27}\), we first need to understand that dividing by a fraction is equivalent to multiplying by its reciprocal.

1. Start with the given expression:
   \[
   \frac{28}{1} \div \frac{30}{27}
   \]

2. Replace the division with multiplication by the reciprocal of \(\frac{30}{27}\):
   \[
   \frac{28}{1} \times \frac{27}{30}
   \]

3. Multiply the numerators together and the denominators together:
   \[
   \frac{28 \times 27}{1 \times 30} = \frac{756}{30}
   \]

4. Simplify the fraction \(\frac{756}{30}\) by finding the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 756 and 30. The GCD of 756 and 30 is 6.

5. Divide both the numerator and the denominator by their GCD:
   \[
   \frac{756 \div 6}{30 \div 6} = \frac{126}{5}
   \]

Thus, the simplified fraction is:
### Answer: \(\frac{126}{5}\)

Expected answer: 126/5

Correct? Yes

\[ \text{Reciprocal of } \frac{15}{9} = \frac{9}{15} \]

\[ \frac{7}{1} \times \frac{9}{15} = \frac{7 \times 9}{1 \times 15} = \frac{63}{15} \]

Now, simplify \( \frac{63}{15} \) by finding the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 63 and 15. The GCD of 63 and 15 is 3.

Divide both the numerator and the denominator by their GCD:
\[ \frac{63 \div 3}{15 \div 3} = \frac{21}{5} \]

Thus, the simplified fraction is:
### Answer: \(\frac{21}{5}\)

ðŸ”— Follow-up

Problem: After finding the solution for the division of fractions (20 / 13) / (17 / 16), now multiply that result by the fraction (20 / 26). Write your answer as a simplified fraction.

Gemma 2B: 

We already found that \(\frac{20}{13} \div \frac{17}{16} = \frac{320}{221}\).

Now, we need to multiply this result by \(\frac{20}{26}\):

\[
\frac{320}{221} \times \frac{20}{26}
\]

First, multiply the numerators together and the denominators together:

\[
\frac{320 \times 20}{221 \times 26} = \frac{6400}{5746}
\]

Next, we simplify the fraction \(\frac{6400}{5746}\). We need to find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 6400 and 5746. 

Using the Euclidean algorithm:
1. \(6400 \div 5746 = 1\) with a remainder of \(654\).
2. \(5746 \div 654 = 8\) with a remainder of \(494\).
3. \(654 \div 494 = 1\) with a remainder of \(160\).
4. \(494 \div 160 = 3\) with a remainder of \(14\).
5. \(160 \div 14 = 11\) with a remainder of \(6\).
6. \(14 \div 6 = 2\) with a remainder of \(2\).
7. \(6 \div 2 = 3\) with a remainder of \(0\).

The GCD is 2.

Now, we divide both the numerator and the denominator by their GCD:

\[
\frac{6400 \div 2}{5746 \div 2} = \frac{3200}{2873}
\]

Thus, the simplified fraction is:

### Answer: \(\frac{3200}{2873}\)

   \[

   \]

   \[
   \frac{570}{552}

   - \(552 \div 18 = 30\) with no remainder

   Therefore, the GCD of 570 and 552 is 18.

   \[
   \frac{570 \div 18}{552 \div 18} = \frac{31.6667}{30.6667} = \frac{95}{92}
   \]

Problem: Evaluate the expression (23 / 26) * (16 / 1) and express your answer as a simplified fraction.

Gemma 2B: 

To evaluate the expression \(\frac{23}{26} \times \frac{16}{1}\), we multiply the numerators together and the denominators together:

\[
\frac{23 \times 16}{26 \times 1}
\]

First, calculate the numerator:

\[
23 \times 16 = 368
\]

Next, calculate the denominator:

\[
26 \times 1 = 26
\]

So, the expression becomes:

\[
\frac{368}{26}
\]

To simplify this fraction, we need to find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 368 and 26. We can use the Euclidean algorithm to find the GCD:

1. Divide 368 by 26 to get the quotient and remainder:
   \[
   368 \div 26 = 14 \quad \text{remainder} \, 4
   \]

2. Now, divide 26 by the remainder 4:
   \[
   26 \div 4 = 6 \quad \text{remainder} \, 2
   \]

3. Next, divide 4 by the remainder 2:
   \[
   4 \div 2 = 2 \quad \text{remainder} \, 0
   \]

Since the remainder is now 0, the GCD is the last non-zero remainder, which is 2.

Now, divide both the numerator and the denominator by their GCD (2):

\[
\frac{368 \div 2}{26 \div 2} = \frac{184}{13}
\]

Thus, the simplified fraction is:

\[
\frac{184}{13}
\]

### Answer: \(\frac{184}{13}\)

Expected answer: 184/13

Correct? Yes

ðŸ”— Follow-up

Problem: Given that you previously calculated (23 / 26) * (16 / 1) as 'g', now find the value of (4 / 7) * g. Express your answer as a simplified fraction.

Gemma 2B: 

We previously calculated \( g = \frac{184}{13} \).

Now, we need to find the value of \( \left(\frac{4}{7}\right) \times g \).

Substitute \( g \) with \(\frac{184}{13}\):

\[
\left(\frac{4}{7}\right) \times \left(\frac{184}{13}\right)
\]

To multiply these fractions, multiply the numerators together and the denominators together:

\[
\frac{4 \times 184}{7 \times 13}
\]

First, calculate the numerator:

\[
4 \times 184 = 736
\]

Next, calculate the denominator:

\[
7 \times 13 = 91
\]

So, the expression becomes:

\[
\frac{736}{91}
\]

To simplify this fraction, we need to check if there is a common divisor between 736 and 91. We can use the Euclidean algorithm to find the GCD:

1. Divide 736 by 91 to get the quotient and remainder:
   \[
   736 \div 91 = 8 \quad \text{remainder} \, 8
   \]

2. Now, divide 91 by the remainder 8:
   \[
   91 \div 8 = 11 \quad \text{remainder} \, 3
   \]

3. Next, divide 8 by the remainder 3:
   \[
   8 \div 3 = 2 \quad \text{remainder} \, 2
   \]

4. Finally, divide 3 by the remainder 2:
   \[
   3 \div 2 = 1 \quad \text{remainder} \, 1
   \]

Since the remainder is now 1, the GCD is 1.

Since the GCD is 1, the fraction \(\frac{736}{91}\) is already in its simplest form.

### Answer: \(\frac{736}{91}\)

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: Compute the following fractional expression: ((21 / 1) / (26 / 20)), express your answer as a simplified fraction.

Gemma 2B: 

To solve the expression \(\left(\frac{21}{1}\right) \div \left(\frac{26}{20}\right)\), we can use the property of division of fractions, which states that dividing by a fraction is equivalent to multiplying by its reciprocal.

First, we find the reciprocal of \(\frac{26}{20}\):
\[
\frac{26}{20} \rightarrow \frac{20}{26}
\]

Next, we multiply \(\frac{21}{1}\) by \(\frac{20}{26}\):
\[
\frac{21}{1} \times \frac{20}{26} = \frac{21 \times 20}{1 \times 26} = \frac{420}{26}
\]

Now, we simplify \(\frac{420}{26}\). We find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 420 and 26, which is 2.

Dividing both the numerator and the denominator by their GCD:
\[
\frac{420 \div 2}{26 \div 2} = \frac{210}{13}
\]

Thus, the simplified form of the expression is:
\[
\frac{210}{13}
\]

### Answer: \(\frac{210}{13}\)

Expected answer: 210/13

Correct? Yes

ðŸ”— Follow-up

Problem: In continuation to the previous problem, let's assume that the value obtained from the expression ((21 / 1) / (26 / 20)) is multiplied by the fraction (21 / 29). What fraction will the result be?

Gemma 2B: 

We previously found that \(\left(\frac{21}{1}\right) \div \left(\frac{26}{20}\right) = \frac{210}{13}\).

Now, we need to multiply this result by the fraction \(\frac{21}{29}\):
\[
\frac{210}{13} \times \frac{21}{29}
\]

To multiply these fractions, we multiply the numerators together and the denominators together:
\[
\frac{210 \times 21}{13 \times 29} = \frac{4410}{377}
\]

Next, we check if the fraction \(\frac{4410}{377}\) can be simplified. We need to find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 4410 and 377. 

Using the Euclidean algorithm:
1. \(4410 \div 377 \approx 11.7\) (integer part is 11)
2. \(4410 - 377 \times 11 = 4410 - 4147 = 263\)
3. \(377 \div 263 \approx 1.43\) (integer part is 1)
4. \(377 - 263 \times 1 = 377 - 263 = 114\)
5. \(263 \div 114 \approx 2.3\) (integer part is 2)
6. \(263 - 114 \times 2 = 263 - 228 = 35\)
7. \(114 \div 35 \approx 3.26\) (integer part is 3)
8. \(114 - 35 \times 3 = 114 - 105 = 9\)
9. \(35 \div 9 \approx 3.89\) (integer part is 3)
10. \(35 - 9 \times 3 = 35 - 27 = 8\)
11. \(9 \div 8 \approx 1.125\) (integer part is 1)
12. \(9 - 8 \times 1 = 9 - 8 = 1\)
13. \(8 \div 1 = 8\) (integer part is 8)
14. \(8 - 1 \times 8 = 8 - 8 = 0\)

The GCD is 1, meaning \(\frac{4410}{377}\) is already in its simplest form.

### Answer: \(\frac{4410}{377}\)

Expected answer: 4410/377

Correct? Yes

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: Jim is baking a cake that calls for 12/2 cups of sugar and 17/14 cups of flour. If Jim needs to multiply the amount of sugar and flour he needs for a larger cake, how much sugar and flour does he need in total? Calculate ((12 / 2) * (17 / 14)) and express your answer as a simplified fraction.

Gemma 2B: 

First, let's simplify the amount of sugar and flour Jim needs for the original cake.

The amount of sugar required is:
\[ \frac{12}{2} = 6 \text{ cups} \]

The amount of flour required is:
\[ \frac{17}{14} \text{ cups} \]

Now, we need to multiply these two quantities together:
\[ 6 \times \frac{17}{14} \]

To perform this multiplication, we can write 6 as a fraction:
\[ 6 = \frac{6}{1} \]

Now, multiply the fractions:
\[ \frac{6}{1} \times \frac{17}{14} = \frac{6 \times 17}{1 \times 14} = \frac{102}{14} \]

Next, we simplify the fraction \(\frac{102}{14}\). We find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 102 and 14, which is 2.

Divide both the numerator and the denominator by their GCD:
\[ \frac{102 \div 2}{14 \div 2} = \frac{51}{7} \]

Thus, the total amount of sugar and flour Jim needs is:
\[ \frac{51}{7} \]

### Answer: \(\frac{51}{7}\)

Expected answer: 51/7

Correct? Yes

ðŸ”— Follow-up

Given that the amount of sugar remains the same at 12/2 cups, how much sugar and flour does he actually need? Calculate ((12 / 2) * (30 / 14)) and express your answer as a simplified fraction.

Gemma 2B: 

First, let's simplify the amount of sugar Jim needs for the cake:

The amount of sugar required is:
\[ \frac{12}{2} = 6 \text{ cups} \]

The corrected amount of flour required is:
\[ \frac{30}{14} \text{ cups} \]

Now, we need to multiply these two quantities together:
\[ 6 \times \frac{30}{14} \]

To perform this multiplication, we can write 6 as a fraction:
\[ 6 = \frac{6}{1} \]

Now, multiply the fractions:
\[ \frac{6}{1} \times \frac{30}{14} = \frac{6 \times 30}{1 \times 14} = \frac{180}{14} \]

Next, we simplify the fraction \(\frac{180}{14}\). We find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 180 and 14, which is 2.

Divide both the numerator and the denominator by their GCD:
\[ \frac{180 \div 2}{14 \div 2} = \frac{90}{7} \]

Thus, the total amount of sugar and flour Jim needs is:
\[ \frac{90}{7} \]

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: Calculate the result of the following operation: ((21 / 16) / (27 / 23)) and represent the answer as a simplified fraction.

Gemma 2B: 

To solve the expression \(\left(\frac{21}{16}\right) \div \left(\frac{27}{23}\right)\), we need to remember that dividing by a fraction is equivalent to multiplying by its reciprocal. Therefore, we can rewrite the expression as:

\[
\left(\frac{21}{16}\right) \div \left(\frac{27}{23}\right) = \left(\frac{21}{16}\right) \times \left(\frac{23}{27}\right)
\]

Next, we multiply the numerators together and the denominators together:

\[
\frac{21 \times 23}{16 \times 27}
\]

Calculating the products:

\[
21 \times 23 = 483
\]
\[
16 \times 27 = 432
\]

So, the expression becomes:

\[
\frac{483}{432}
\]

To simplify this fraction, we need to find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 483 and 432. We can use the Euclidean algorithm to find the GCD:

1. \(483 \div 432 = 1\) with a remainder of \(51\)
2. \(432 \div 51 = 8\) with a remainder of \(24\)
3. \(51 \div 24 = 2\) with a remainder of \(3\)
4. \(24 \div 3 = 8\) with a remainder of \(0\)

The GCD is \(3\).

Now, we divide both the numerator and the denominator by their GCD:

\[
\frac{483 \div 3}{432 \div 3} = \frac{161}{144}
\]

Thus, the simplified fraction is:

\[
\frac{161}{144}
\]

### Answer: \(\frac{161}{144}\)

Expected answer: 161/144

Correct? Yes

\]

So, the expression becomes:

\frac{25921}{20736}

1. \(25921 \div 20736 = 1\) with a remainder of \(5185\)
2. \(20736 \div 5185 = 4\) with a remainder of \(1\)
3. \(5185 \div 1 = 5185\) with a remainder of \(0\)

The GCD is \(1\), which means the fraction \(\frac{25921}{20736}\) is already in its simplest form.

Problem: Calculate the result of the following operation: (12 / 14) * (28 / 5). Simplify the resulting fraction to its lowest terms.

Gemma 2B: 

First, we start by performing the multiplication of the two fractions:

\[
\left( \frac{12}{14} \right) \times \left( \frac{28}{5} \right)
\]

To multiply fractions, we multiply the numerators together and the denominators together:

\[
\frac{12 \times 28}{14 \times 5}
\]

Next, we calculate the products in the numerator and the denominator:

\[
12 \times 28 = 336
\]
\[
14 \times 5 = 70
\]

So, the fraction becomes:

\[
\frac{336}{70}
\]

Now, we need to simplify this fraction to its lowest terms. We do this by finding the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 336 and 70. 

First, we find the prime factorizations of both numbers:
- The prime factorization of 336 is \( 2^4 \times 3 \times 7 \).
- The prime factorization of 70 is \( 2 \times 5 \times 7 \).

The common factors are \( 2 \) and \( 7 \). Therefore, the GCD is:

\[
2 \times 7 = 14
\]

We divide both the numerator and the denominator by their GCD (14):

\[
\frac{336 \div 14}{70 \div 14} = \frac{24}{5}
\]

Thus, the simplified fraction is:

\[
\frac{24}{5}
\]

\[
\left( \frac{3}{14} \right) \times \left( \frac{28}{5} \right)
\]

To multiply fractions, we multiply the numerators together and the denominators together:

\[
\frac{3 \times 28}{14 \times 5}
\]

Next, we calculate the products in the numerator and the denominator:

\[
3 \times 28 = 84
\]
\[
14 \times 5 = 70
\]

So, the fraction becomes:

\[
\frac{84}{70}
\]

Now, we need to simplify this fraction to its lowest terms. We do this by finding the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 84 and 70. 

First, we find the prime factorizations of both numbers:
- The prime factorization of 84 is \( 2^2 \times 3 \times 7 \).
- The prime factorization of 70 is \( 2 \times 5 \times 7 \).

The common factors are \( 2 \) and \( 7 \). Therefore, the GCD is:

\[
2 \times 7 = 14
\]

We divide both the numerator and the denominator by their GCD (14):

\[
\frac{84 \div 14}{70 \div 14} = \frac{6}{5}
\]

Thus, the simplified fraction is:

\[
\frac{6}{5}
\]

### Answer: \(\frac{6}{5}\)

Expected answer: 6/5

Correct? Yes

\[

\]

Next, we simplify the fraction \(\frac{1596}{256}\). To do this, we need to find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 1596 and 256.

1. Prime factorization of 1596:
   - 1596 is even, so divide by 2: \(1596 \div 2 = 798\)
   - 798 is even, so divide by 2: \(798 \div 2 = 399\)
   - 399 is divisible by 3: \(399 \div 3 = 133\)
   - 133 is divisible by 7: \(133 \div 7 = 19\)
   - 19 is a prime number.

   Therefore, the prime factorization of 1596 is \(2^2 \times 3 \times 7 \times 19\).

2. Prime factorization of 256:
   - 256 is a power of 2: \(256 = 2^8\).

The common factors are \(2^2\). Therefore, the GCD of 1596 and 256 is \(2^2 = 4\).

Now, divide both the numerator and the denominator by their GCD (4):

\[
\frac{1596 \div 4}{256 \div 4} = \frac{399}{64}
\]

The fraction \(\frac{399}{64}\) is already in its simplest form.

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: Calculate the value of the expression ((29 / 17) / (27 / 22)). Write your answer as a simplified fraction.

Gemma 2B: 

To solve the expression \(\left(\frac{29}{17}\right) \div \left(\frac{27}{22}\right)\), we can use the property of division of fractions, which states that dividing by a fraction is equivalent to multiplying by its reciprocal.

First, we find the reciprocal of \(\frac{27}{22}\), which is \(\frac{22}{27}\).

Now, we rewrite the expression as:
\[
\left(\frac{29}{17}\right) \times \left(\frac{22}{27}\right)
\]

Next, we multiply the numerators together and the denominators together:
\[
\frac{29 \times 22}{17 \times 27}
\]

Calculating the products:
\[
29 \times 22 = 638
\]
\[
17 \times 27 = 459
\]

So, the expression simplifies to:
\[
\frac{638}{459}
\]

To simplify this fraction, we need to find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 638 and 459. Using the Euclidean algorithm:

1. \(638 \div 459\) gives a quotient of 1 and a remainder of \(638 - 459 = 179\).
2. \(459 \div 179\) gives a quotient of 2 and a remainder of \(459 - 2 \times 179 = 101\).
3. \(179 \div 101\) gives a quotient of 1 and a remainder of \(179 - 101 = 78\).
4. \(101 \div 78\) gives a quotient of 1 and a remainder of \(101 - 78 = 23\).
5. \(78 \div 23\) gives a quotient of 3 and a remainder of \(78 - 3 \times 23 = 9\).
6. \(23 \div 9\) gives a quotient of 2 and a remainder of \(23 - 2 \times 9 = 5\).
7. \(9 \div 5\) gives a quotient of 1 and a remainder of \(9 - 5 = 4\).
8. \(5 \div 4\) gives a quotient of 1 and a remainder of \(5 - 4 = 1\).
9. \(4 \div 1\) gives a quotient of 4 and a remainder of \(4 - 4 = 0\).

The GCD is 1. Therefore, the fraction \(\frac{638}{459}\) is already in its simplest form.

### Answer: \(\frac{638}{459}\)

Expected answer: 638/459

Correct? Yes

ðŸ”— Follow-up

Gemma 2B:

\[
638 \times 27 = 17226
\]
\[
459 \times 2 = 918
\]

So, the expression simplifies to:

\[
\frac{17226}{918}
\]

To simplify this fraction, we need to find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 17226 and 918. Using the Euclidean algorithm:

1. \(17226 \div 918\) gives a quotient of 18 and a remainder of \(17226 - 918 \times 18 = 0\).

Since the remainder is 0, the GCD is 918.

Now, we divide both the numerator and the denominator by their GCD:

\[
\frac{17226 \div 918}{918 \div 918} = \frac{18}{1}

Thus, the simplified fraction is:

Now, we need to simplify this fraction. We find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 1100 and 624. The prime factorization of 1100 is \( 2^2 \times 5^2 \times 11 \), and the prime factorization of 624 is \( 2^4 \times 3 \times 13 \). The common factor is \( 2^2 = 4 \).

Divide both the numerator and the denominator by their GCD, which is 4:

\[
\frac{1100 \div 4}{624 \div 4} = \frac{275}{156}
\]

Since 275 and 156 have no common factors other than 1, the fraction is already in its simplest form.

Problem: After evaluating the expression ((20 / 22) * (14 / 11)), multiply your result by (17/3). Write your final answer as a simplified fraction.

Gemma 2B: 

We previously evaluated the expression \(\left(\frac{20}{22}\right) \times \left(\frac{14}{11}\right)\) and found it to be \(\frac{140}{121}\).

Now, we need to multiply this result by \(\frac{17}{3}\):
\[
\frac{140}{121} \times \frac{17}{3} = \frac{140 \times 17}{121 \times 3}
\]

First, calculate the numerator:
\[
140 \times 17 = 2380
\]

Next, calculate the denominator:
\[
121 \times 3 = 363
\]

So, the product is:
\[
\frac{2380}{363}
\]

Now, we need to simplify this fraction. To do this, we find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 2380 and 363. 

Using the Euclidean algorithm:
1. \(2380 \div 363 \approx 6\) with a remainder of \(2380 - 6 \times 363 = 2380 - 2178 = 202\).
2. \(363 \div 202 \approx 1\) with a remainder of \(363 - 202 = 161\).
3. \(202 \div 161 \approx 1\) with a remainder of \(202 - 161 = 41\).
4. \(161 \div 41 \approx 3\) with a remainder of \(161 - 3 \times 41 = 161 - 123 = 38\).
5. \(41 \div 38 \approx 1\) with a remainder of \(41 - 38 = 3\).
6. \(38 \div 3 \approx 12\) with a remainder of \(38 - 12 \times 3 = 38 - 36 = 2\).
7. \(3 \div 2 \approx 1\) with a remainder of \(3 - 2 = 1\).
8. \(2 \div 1 \approx 2\) with a remainder of \(2 - 2 \times 1 = 2 - 2 = 0\).

The GCD is 1, so the fraction \(\frac{2380}{363}\) is already in its simplest form.

### Answer: \(\frac{2380}{363}\)

Gemma 2B: 

To find the result of \(\left(\frac{75}{32} \times \frac{29}{23}\right)\), we follow these steps:

1. Multiply the numerators together:
   \[
   75 \times 29 = 2175
   \]

2. Multiply the denominators together:
   \[
   32 \times 23 = 736
   \]

3. Combine the results to form a single fraction:
   \[
   \frac{2175}{736}
   \]

4. Simplify the fraction if possible. We need to check if 2175 and 736 have any common factors. 

First, let's find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 2175 and 736. Using the Euclidean algorithm:

\[
2175 \div 736 \approx 2.955 \quad \text{(integer part is 2)}
\]
\[
2175 - 2 \times 736 = 2175 - 1472 = 703
\]

Next, apply the Euclidean algorithm to 736 and 703:

\[
736 \div 703 \approx 1.047 \quad \text{(integer part is 1)}
\]
\[
736 - 1 \times 703 = 736 - 703 = 33
\]

Next, apply the Euclidean algorithm to 703 and 33:

\[
703 \div 33 \approx 21.303 \quad \text{(integer part is 21)}
\]
\[
703 - 21 \times 33 = 703 - 693 = 10
\]

Next, apply the Euclidean algorithm to 33 and 10:

\[
33 \div 10 \approx 3.3 \quad \text{(integer part is 3)}
\]
\[
33 - 3 \times 10 = 33 - 30 = 3
\]

Finally, apply the Euclidean algorithm to 10 and 3:

\[
10 \div 3 \approx 3.333 \quad \text{(integer part is 3)}
\]
\[
10 - 3 \times 3 = 10 - 9 = 1
\]

Since the GCD is 1, the fraction \(\frac{2175}{736}\) is already in its simplest form.

Thus, the simplified fraction is \(\frac{2175}{736}\).

In terms of the original division or portion sharing scenario, this additional operation represents further distributing or scaling the portions. If \(\frac{75}{32}\) was the portion each group received initially, multiplying by \(\frac{29}{23}\) adjusts the portion size by a factor of \(\frac{29}{23}\), either increasing or decreasing the amount each group gets based on the value of the fraction.

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: What is the result when you multiply (29/17) by (26/15)?

Gemma 2B: 

To find the result of multiplying \(\frac{29}{17}\) by \(\frac{26}{15}\), we multiply the numerators together and the denominators together:

\[
\frac{29}{17} \times \frac{26}{15} = \frac{29 \times 26}{17 \times 15}
\]

First, calculate the numerator:

\[
29 \times 26 = 754
\]

Next, calculate the denominator:

\[
17 \times 15 = 255
\]

So, the product is:

\[
\frac{754}{255}
\]

To simplify this fraction, we need to find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 754 and 255. We can use the Euclidean algorithm to find the GCD.

1. Divide 754 by 255 and find the remainder:
\[
754 \div 255 \approx 2 \quad \text{(quotient)} \quad \text{remainder} = 754 - 2 \times 255 = 244
\]

2. Divide 255 by 244 and find the remainder:
\[
255 \div 244 \approx 1 \quad \text{(quotient)} \quad \text{remainder} = 255 - 1 \times 244 = 11
\]

3. Divide 244 by 11 and find the remainder:
\[
244 \div 11 \approx 22 \quad \text{(quotient)} \quad \text{remainder} = 244 - 22 \times 11 = 2
\]

4. Divide 11 by 2 and find the remainder:
\[
11 \div 2 \approx 5 \quad \text{(quotient)} \quad \text{remainder} = 11 - 5 \times 2 = 1
\]

5. Divide 2 by 1 and find the remainder:
\[
2 \div 1 \approx 2 \quad \text{(quotient)} \quad \text{remainder} = 2 - 2 \times 1 = 0
\]

Since the remainder is now 0, the GCD is the last non-zero remainder, which is 1. Therefore, the fraction \(\frac{754}{255}\) is already in its simplest form.

### Answer: \(\frac{754}{255}\)

Expected answer: 754/255

Correct? Yes

\]

First, calculate the numerator:

\[
754 \times 21 = 15834
\]

Next, calculate the denominator:

\[
255 \times 9 = 2295
\]

So, the product is:

\[
\frac{15834}{2295}
\]

To simplify this fraction, we need to find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 15834 and 2295. We can use the Euclidean algorithm to find the GCD.

1. Divide 15834 by 2295 and find the remainder:
\[
15834 \div 2295 \approx 6 \quad \text{(quotient)} \quad \text{remainder} = 15834 - 6 \times 2295 = 1954
\]

2. Divide 2295 by 1954 and find the remainder:
\[
2295 \div 1954 \approx 1 \quad \text{(quotient)} \quad \text{remainder} = 2295 - 1 \times 1954 = 341
\]

3. Divide 1954 by 341 and find the remainder:
\[
1954 \div 341 \approx 5 \quad \text{(quotient)} \quad \text{remainder} = 1954 - 5 \times 341 = 249
\]

4. Divide 341 by 249 and find the remainder:
\[
341 \div 249 \approx 1 \quad \text{(quotient)} \quad \text{remainder} = 341 - 1 \times 249 = 92
\]

5. Divide 249 by 92 and find the remainder:
\[
249 \div 92 \approx 2 \quad \text{(quotient)} \quad \text{remainder} = 249 - 2 \times 92 = 65
\]

6. Divide 92 by 65 and find the remainder:
\[
92 \div 65 \approx 1 \quad \text{(quotient)} \quad \text{remainder} = 92 - 1 \times 65 = 27
\]

7. Divide 65 by 27 and find the remainder:
\[
65 \div 27 \approx 2 \quad \text{(quotient)} \quad \text{remainder} = 65 - 2 \times 27 = 11
\]

8. Divide 27 by 11 and find the remainder:
\[
27 \div 11 \approx 2 \quad \text{(quotient)} \quad \text{remainder} = 27 - 2 \times 11 = 5
\]

9. Divide 11 by 5 and find the remainder:
\[
11 \div 5 \approx 2 \quad \text{(quotient)} \quad \text{remainder} = 11 - 2 \times 5 = 1
\]

10. Divide 5 by 1 and find the remainder:
\[
5 \div 1 \approx 5 \quad \text{(quotient)} \quad \text{remainder} = 5 - 5 \times 1 = 0
\]

Since the remainder is now 0, the GCD is the last non-zero remainder, which is 1. Therefore, the fraction \(\frac{15834}{2295}\) is already in its simplest form.

### Answer: \(\frac{15834}{2295}\)

Expected answer: 5278/765

Problem: If the original fraction were (15/17) instead of (29/17), what would be the result when you multiply (15/17) by (26/15)?

Gemma 2B: 

To find the result of multiplying \(\frac{15}{17}\) by \(\frac{26}{15}\), we multiply the numerators together and the denominators together:

\[
\frac{15}{17} \times \frac{26}{15} = \frac{15 \times 26}{17 \times 15}
\]

First, calculate the numerator:

\[
15 \times 26 = 390
\]

Next, calculate the denominator:

\[
17 \times 15 = 255
\]

So, the product is:

\[
\frac{390}{255}
\]

To simplify this fraction, we need to find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 390 and 255. We can use the Euclidean algorithm to find the GCD.

1. Divide 390 by 255 and find the remainder:
\[
390 \div 255 \approx 1 \quad \text{(quotient)} \quad \text{remainder} = 390 - 1 \times 255 = 135
\]

2. Divide 255 by 135 and find the remainder:
\[
255 \div 135 \approx 1 \quad \text{(quotient)} \quad \text{remainder} = 255 - 1 \times 135 = 120
\]

3. Divide 135 by 120 and find the remainder:
\[
135 \div 120 \approx 1 \quad \text{(quotient)} \quad \text{remainder} = 135 - 1 \times 120 = 15
\]

4. Divide 120 by 15 and find the remainder:
\[
120 \div 15 \approx 8 \quad \text{(quotient)} \quad \text{remainder} = 120 - 8 \times 15 = 0
\]

Since the remainder is now 0, the GCD is the last non-zero remainder, which is 15. Therefore, we can simplify the fraction \(\frac{390}{255}\) by dividing both the numerator and the denominator by 15:

\[
\frac{390 \div 15}{255 \div 15} = \frac{26}{17}
\]

   \]

   \[

   \]

\[
\frac{230}{48}

\[

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: Calculate the result of the following multiplication of fractions: (21 / 26) * (20 / 9). Write your answer in simplest form.

Gemma 2B: 

To solve the multiplication of the fractions \(\frac{21}{26} \times \frac{20}{9}\), we follow these steps:

1. Multiply the numerators together:
\[ 21 \times 20 = 420 \]

2. Multiply the denominators together:
\[ 26 \times 9 = 234 \]

So, the product of the fractions is:
\[ \frac{420}{234} \]

Next, we need to simplify this fraction. To do this, we find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 420 and 234.

First, we find the prime factorizations of both numbers:
- The prime factorization of 420 is \( 2^2 \times 3 \times 5 \times 7 \)
- The prime factorization of 234 is \( 2 \times 3^2 \times 13 \)

The common prime factors are 2 and 3. Therefore, the GCD is:
\[ 2 \times 3 = 6 \]

Now, we divide both the numerator and the denominator by their GCD:
\[ \frac{420 \div 6}{234 \div 6} = \frac{70}{39} \]

Thus, the simplified form of the fraction is:
\[ \frac{70}{39} \]

### Answer: \(\frac{70}{39}\)

Expected answer: 70/39

Correct? Yes

\]

\[

\]

\[

\]

2. \(78 \div 21 = 3\) with a remainder of \(78 - 3 \times 21 = 15\)

5. \(6 \div 3 = 2\) with a remainder of \(6 - 2 \times 3 = 0\)

The GCD is the last non-zero remainder, which is 3.

Now, we divide both the numerator and the denominator by their GCD:

\[
\frac{255 \div 3}{78 \div 3} = \frac{85}{26}
\]

Thus, the simplified fraction is:

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: Calculate the result of the following equation: (25 / 18) * (17 / 6). Write your answer as a simplified fraction.

Gemma 2B: 

To solve the equation \(\left(\frac{25}{18}\right) \times \left(\frac{17}{6}\right)\), we multiply the numerators together and the denominators together:

\[
\frac{25 \times 17}{18 \times 6}
\]

First, calculate the numerator:

\[
25 \times 17 = 425
\]

Next, calculate the denominator:

\[
18 \times 6 = 108
\]

So, the fraction is:

\[
\frac{425}{108}
\]

To simplify this fraction, we need to find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 425 and 108. We can use the Euclidean algorithm to find the GCD.

1. Divide 425 by 108 to get the remainder:
\[
425 \div 108 \approx 3 \quad \text{(remainder 101)}
\]

2. Now, divide 108 by 101 to get the remainder:
\[
108 \div 101 \approx 1 \quad \text{(remainder 7)}
\]

3. Next, divide 101 by 7 to get the remainder:
\[
101 \div 7 \approx 14 \quad \text{(remainder 3)}
\]

4. Then, divide 7 by 3 to get the remainder:
\[
7 \div 3 \approx 2 \quad \text{(remainder 1)}
\]

5. Finally, divide 3 by 1 to get the remainder:
\[
3 \div 1 = 3 \quad \text{(remainder 0)}
\]

Since the remainder is now 0, the GCD is the last non-zero remainder, which is 1. Therefore, the fraction \(\frac{425}{108}\) is already in its simplest form.

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: Calculate the result of multiplying 9 (which is a fraction equivalent to 9/1) by 2/17. Write your answer as a simplified fraction.

Gemma 2B: 

To calculate the result of multiplying \( \frac{9}{1} \) by \( \frac{2}{17} \), we use the rule for multiplying fractions:

\[
\frac{a}{b} \times \frac{c}{d} = \frac{a \times c}{b \times d}
\]

Here, \( a = 9 \), \( b = 1 \), \( c = 2 \), and \( d = 17 \). Substituting these values into the formula, we get:

\[
\frac{9}{1} \times \frac{2}{17} = \frac{9 \times 2}{1 \times 17} = \frac{18}{17}
\]

The fraction \( \frac{18}{17} \) is already in its simplest form because 18 and 17 have no common factors other than 1.

### Answer: \(\frac{18}{17}\)

Expected answer: 18/17

Correct? Yes

Next, we need to simplify this fraction by finding the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 8721 and 4508.

- The prime factorization of 8721 is \(3 \times 2907\), and further factorizing 2907 gives \(3 \times 969\), and further factorizing 969 gives \(3 \times 323\), and further factorizing 323 gives \(17 \times 19\). So, \(8721 = 3^3 \times 17 \times 19\).
- The prime factorization of 4508 is \(2^2 \times 1127\). 

Since there are no common factors between 8721 and 4508 other than 1, the fraction \(\frac{8721}{4508}\) is already in its simplest form.

### Answer: \(\frac{8721}{4508}\)

Expected answer: 8721/4508

Correct? Yes

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: Calculate the result of the following fraction multiplication: (16 / 3) * (25 / 26)

Gemma 2B: 

To solve the multiplication of the fractions \(\frac{16}{3} \times \frac{25}{26}\), we multiply the numerators together and the denominators together.

First, multiply the numerators:
\[ 16 \times 25 = 400 \]

Next, multiply the denominators:
\[ 3 \times 26 = 78 \]

So, the product of the fractions is:
\[ \frac{400}{78} \]

To simplify this fraction, we need to find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 400 and 78. We can use the Euclidean algorithm to find the GCD.

1. Divide 400 by 78 and find the remainder:
\[ 400 \div 78 = 5 \text{ remainder } 10 \]
2. Now, divide 78 by the remainder 10:
\[ 78 \div 10 = 7 \text{ remainder } 8 \]
3. Next, divide 10 by the remainder 8:
\[ 10 \div 8 = 1 \text{ remainder } 2 \]
4. Finally, divide 8 by the remainder 2:
\[ 8 \div 2 = 4 \text{ remainder } 0 \]

Since the remainder is now 0, the GCD is the last non-zero remainder, which is 2.

Now, divide both the numerator and the denominator of \(\frac{400}{78}\) by their GCD, which is 2:
\[ \frac{400 \div 2}{78 \div 2} = \frac{200}{39} \]

### Answer: \(\frac{200}{39}\)

Expected answer: 200/39

Correct? Yes

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: What is the fraction you get when you multiply (16 / 6) with (29 / 27)? Write your answer in simplest form.

Gemma 2B: 

To find the fraction resulting from the multiplication of \(\frac{16}{6}\) and \(\frac{29}{27}\), we follow these steps:

1. Multiply the numerators:
\[
16 \times 29 = 464
\]

2. Multiply the denominators:
\[
6 \times 27 = 162
\]

So, the product of the fractions is:
\[
\frac{464}{162}
\]

Next, we simplify this fraction by finding the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 464 and 162. We can use the Euclidean algorithm to find the GCD.

First, divide 464 by 162 and find the remainder:
\[
464 \div 162 \approx 2 \quad \text{(quotient)} \quad \text{remainder} = 464 - 2 \times 162 = 464 - 324 = 140
\]

Next, divide 162 by 140:
\[
162 \div 140 \approx 1 \quad \text{(quotient)} \quad \text{remainder} = 162 - 1 \times 140 = 162 - 140 = 22
\]

Next, divide 140 by 22:
\[
140 \div 22 \approx 6 \quad \text{(quotient)} \quad \text{remainder} = 140 - 6 \times 22 = 140 - 132 = 8
\]

Next, divide 22 by 8:
\[
22 \div 8 \approx 2 \quad \text{(quotient)} \quad \text{remainder} = 22 - 2 \times 8 = 22 - 16 = 6
\]

Next, divide 8 by 6:
\[
8 \div 6 \approx 1 \quad \text{(quotient)} \quad \text{remainder} = 8 - 1 \times 6 = 8 - 6 = 2
\]

Finally, divide 6 by 2:
\[
6 \div 2 \approx 3 \quad \text{(quotient)} \quad \text{remainder} = 6 - 3 \times 2 = 6 - 6 = 0
\]

Since the remainder is now 0, the GCD of 464 and 162 is 2.

Now, we simplify \(\frac{464}{162}\) by dividing both the numerator and the denominator by their GCD, which is 2:
\[
\frac{464 \div 2}{162 \div 2} = \frac{232}{81}
\]

Thus, the fraction in simplest form is:
\[
\frac{232}{81}
\]

### Answer: \(\frac{232}{81}\)

Expected answer: 232/81

Gemma 2B:

Problem: If a car consumes 16/10 gallons of petrol every mile and you have to drive a route that is 13/17 of a mile long, how many gallons of petrol will the car have consumed when you finish the drive? Express your answer as a simplified fraction.

Gemma 2B: 

To determine the amount of petrol consumed, we need to multiply the petrol consumption rate per mile by the distance driven.

The petrol consumption rate is given as \(\frac{16}{10}\) gallons per mile, and the distance is \(\frac{13}{17}\) of a mile.

First, we multiply these two fractions:

\[
\frac{16}{10} \times \frac{13}{17}
\]

To multiply fractions, we multiply the numerators together and the denominators together:

\[
\frac{16 \times 13}{10 \times 17} = \frac{208}{170}
\]

Next, we simplify the fraction \(\frac{208}{170}\). We find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 208 and 170. The GCD of 208 and 170 is 2.

We divide both the numerator and the denominator by their GCD:

\[
\frac{208 \div 2}{170 \div 2} = \frac{104}{85}
\]

We check if \(\frac{104}{85}\) can be simplified further. The GCD of 104 and 85 is 1, so the fraction is already in its simplest form.

### Answer: \(\frac{104}{85}\)

Expected answer: 104/85

Correct? Yes

\frac{16}{10} \times \frac{13}{7}
\]

To multiply fractions, we multiply the numerators together and the denominators together:

\[
\frac{16 \times 13}{10 \times 7} = \frac{208}{70}
\]

Next, we simplify the fraction \(\frac{208}{70}\). We find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 208 and 70. The GCD of 208 and 70 is 2.

We divide both the numerator and the denominator by their GCD:

\[
\frac{208 \div 2}{70 \div 2} = \frac{104}{35}
\]

We check if \(\frac{104}{35}\) can be simplified further. The GCD of 104 and 35 is 1, so the fraction is already in its simplest form.

### Answer: \(\frac{104}{35}\)

Expected answer: 104/35

Correct? Yes

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: Calculate the result of the following problem and express your answer as a simplified fraction: (29 / 10) / (18 / 16)

Gemma 2B: 

To solve the problem \(\frac{29}{10} \div \frac{18}{16}\), we can use the property of division of fractions, which states that dividing by a fraction is equivalent to multiplying by its reciprocal.

First, we find the reciprocal of \(\frac{18}{16}\):
\[
\text{Reciprocal of } \frac{18}{16} = \frac{16}{18}
\]

Next, we multiply \(\frac{29}{10}\) by \(\frac{16}{18}\):
\[
\frac{29}{10} \times \frac{16}{18}
\]

We multiply the numerators together and the denominators together:
\[
\frac{29 \times 16}{10 \times 18} = \frac{464}{180}
\]

Now, we need to simplify the fraction \(\frac{464}{180}\). We do this by finding the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 464 and 180. 

First, we find the prime factorizations:
- 464: \(2^4 \times 29\)
- 180: \(2^2 \times 3^2 \times 5\)

The common factors are \(2^2\), so the GCD is \(2^2 = 4\).

We divide both the numerator and the denominator by their GCD:
\[
\frac{464 \div 4}{180 \div 4} = \frac{116}{45}
\]

Thus, the simplified fraction is:
\[
\frac{116}{45}
\]

### Answer: \(\frac{116}{45}\)

Expected answer: 116/45

Correct? Yes

ðŸ”— Follow-up

Gemma 2B:

\frac{116}{45} \times \frac{8}{17}

\frac{116 \times 8}{45 \times 17} = \frac{928}{765}

Next, we simplify the fraction \(\frac{928}{765}\). We do this by finding the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 928 and 765.

First, we find the prime factorizations:
- 928: \(2^4 \times 58\)
- 765: \(3 \times 5 \times 17\)

Since there are no common prime factors between 928 and 765, the GCD is 1.

Thus, the fraction \(\frac{928}{765}\) is already in its simplest form.

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: Jeremy is trying to solve a complex fraction problem. He needs to find out the result of multiplying (15/12) by (27/3). Can you help Jeremy solve this problem? Write your answer as a simplified fraction.

Gemma 2B: 

To solve the problem of multiplying \(\frac{15}{12}\) by \(\frac{27}{3}\), we follow these steps:

1. Multiply the numerators together:
\[ 15 \times 27 = 405 \]

2. Multiply the denominators together:
\[ 12 \times 3 = 36 \]

So, the product of the fractions is:
\[ \frac{405}{36} \]

Next, we need to simplify this fraction. We do this by finding the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 405 and 36.

First, we find the prime factorizations:
- 405: \( 405 = 5 \times 3^4 \)
- 36: \( 36 = 2^2 \times 3^2 \)

The common prime factor is \(3\), and the lowest power of \(3\) in both factorizations is \(3^2\).

Thus, the GCD is:
\[ 3^2 = 9 \]

Now, we divide both the numerator and the denominator by their GCD:
\[ \frac{405 \div 9}{36 \div 9} = \frac{45}{4} \]

So, the simplified fraction is:
\[ \frac{45}{4} \]

### Answer: \(\frac{45}{4}\)

Expected answer: 45/4

Correct? Yes

Gemma 2B:

\[ 45 \times 22 = 990 \]

2. Multiply the denominators together:
\[ 4 \times 14 = 56 \]

So, the product of the fractions is:
\[ \frac{990}{56} \]

Next, we need to simplify this fraction. We do this by finding the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 990 and 56.

First, we find the prime factorizations:
- 990: \( 990 = 2 \times 3^2 \times 5 \times 11 \)
- 56: \( 56 = 2^3 \times 7 \)

The common prime factor is \(2\), and the lowest power of \(2\) in both factorizations is \(2\).

Thus, the GCD is:
\[ 2 \]

Now, we divide both the numerator and the denominator by their GCD:
\[ \frac{990 \div 2}{56 \div 2} = \frac{495}{28} \]

Next, we check if \(\frac{495}{28}\) can be simplified further. We need to find the GCD of 495 and 28.

Prime factorizations:
- 495: \( 495 = 3^2 \times 5 \times 11 \)
- 28: \( 28 = 2^2 \times 7 \)

There are no common prime factors between 495 and 28, so the fraction \(\frac{495}{28}\) is already in its simplest form.

Problem: Jeremy realized he made a mistake in his calculations. Instead of multiplying the fraction (15/12) by (27/3) as previously thought, he actually needs to multiply it by (27/5). What is the resulting simplified fraction, now that Jeremy has corrected his mistake?

Gemma 2B: 

To solve the problem of multiplying \(\frac{15}{12}\) by \(\frac{27}{5}\), we follow these steps:

1. Multiply the numerators together:
\[ 15 \times 27 = 405 \]

2. Multiply the denominators together:
\[ 12 \times 5 = 60 \]

So, the product of the fractions is:
\[ \frac{405}{60} \]

Next, we need to simplify this fraction. We do this by finding the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 405 and 60.

First, we find the prime factorizations:
- 405: \( 405 = 5 \times 3^4 \)
- 60: \( 60 = 2^2 \times 3 \times 5 \)

The common prime factors are \(3\) and \(5\), and the lowest power of each common factor is:
- \(3^1\)
- \(5^1\)

Thus, the GCD is:
\[ 3 \times 5 = 15 \]

Now, we divide both the numerator and the denominator by their GCD:
\[ \frac{405 \div 15}{60 \div 15} = \frac{27}{4} \]

So, the simplified fraction is:
\[ \frac{27}{4} \]

### Answer: \(\frac{27}{4}\)

Expected answer: 27/4

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: Find the result of ((28 / 6) * (16 / 24)). Write your answer as a simplified fraction.

Gemma 2B: 

First, we simplify each fraction individually:

\[
\frac{28}{6} = \frac{28 \div 2}{6 \div 2} = \frac{14}{3}
\]

\[
\frac{16}{24} = \frac{16 \div 8}{24 \div 8} = \frac{2}{3}
\]

Next, we multiply the simplified fractions:

\[
\left( \frac{14}{3} \right) \times \left( \frac{2}{3} \right) = \frac{14 \times 2}{3 \times 3} = \frac{28}{9}
\]

The fraction \(\frac{28}{9}\) is already in its simplest form.

### Answer: \(\frac{28}{9}\)

Expected answer: 28/9
